    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer10497321274611050499">Publishers note:<br/><br/>The Octunnumi does not exist.<br/><br/>Fosbit and any files relating to a Fosbit do not exist.<br/><br/>The Tarelen peoples that protect and provide sanctuary for the Avitens of Fethrist are not real.<br/><br/>The abilities of the Tarelen peoples with their heightened skills, living in their Utopian world are myth, their purpose here mere tales; rumours of their reincarnations enabling </span>
  <span id="freeText10497321274611050499" style="display:none">Publishers note:<br /><br />The Octunnumi does not exist.<br /><br />Fosbit and any files relating to a Fosbit do not exist.<br /><br />The Tarelen peoples that protect and provide sanctuary for the Avitens of Fethrist are not real.<br /><br />The abilities of the Tarelen peoples with their heightened skills, living in their Utopian world are myth, their purpose here mere tales; rumours of their reincarnations enabling them to live many lives… ridiculous!<br /><br />And there is definitely no magic.<br /><br />None at all.<br /><br />No, really, there isn’t.<br /><br />Magic is not a thing.<br /><br />There are also no hidden worlds or mythical beings coexisting just out of sight. <br /><br />Equally, there are no secret access points to these hidden worlds that don’t exist, and there is no, 'unfinished business from the past' that is set to destroy, well, anything. <br /><br />There is no disaster looming.<br /><br />Anyway, regardless of any potential threat that may or may not be present, this publication, The Octunnumi and any reference to any other beings is a work of fiction.<br /><br />And for the record, Scariodintts, should they exist, are perfectly lovely beings whose purpose in life is grossly misunderstood.</span>

      </div>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1954218-where-is-the-hardback-edition">Where is the hardback edition?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1954218'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F40034669-the-octunnumi-fosbit-files-prologue">like</a></span>

<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/1954218-where-is-the-hardback-edition">23 days ago</a>
</li>

<a href="/questions/1954218-where-is-the-hardback-edition">Add your answer</a>
</li>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/81712102-trevor-foris"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1575624449i/81712102._UX100_CR0,25,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/81712102-trevor-foris">Trevor Foris</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Hello lovely being…<br/><br/>Patrick, thank you so much for your message. We hope we find you and yours all safe and well.<br/><br/>Due to the complexities and special fi<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Hello lovely being…<br /><br />Patrick, thank you so much for your message. We hope we find you and yours all safe and well.<br /><br />Due to the complexities and special finishes of The Octunnumi cover, it was not possible to produce a hardback edition to the standard that the book demanded, so we developed a hybrid version of hard and paper back. <br /><br />Measuring 15.4 x 23 x 4.5cm, The Octunnumi commands the attention of a hard back – the heavier grade board we have used for the cover provides stability and impact whilst allowing us to have a combination of embossing, spot uv, foiling and soft touch laminate as an awesome finish. This also enabled us to incorporate the fabulous AR features via our free app.<br /><br />However, plans are afoot to publish a special edition which will be in hardback and have many unique features exclusive to itself. Unfortunately, due to the current unsettling times we are unable to put a date on this.<br /><br />In the meantime, do please consider the hybrid version available from our website <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.the-octunnumi.com">www.the-octunnumi.com</a> you will not be disappointed. To quote our blurb, 'The Octunnumi is not for everyone - some just don’t get it and thats fine… it would not do at all if we all liked the same things now, would it - but if you like your fantasy epic, twisty, turny, puzzling and compelling, a little complex and a challenge to the intellect with many, not so obvious layers, then you are our kind of being and you are just going to love being a being that is part of a community of like-minded beings that gets it – if nothing else, even if you hate it there are always the continuing after-sale additions of the superb AR to keep it interesting. And if all else fails, the design is sooo beautiful, the book sooo big, it would make a fantastical doorstop!'<br /><br />I do hope this answers your question. Should you have any further queries do please drop us a line we would love to hear from you.<br /><br /><br />Thank you again for your message.<br /><br />Stay safe.<br />The Octunnumi Team<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_2442030865" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2442030865" />
    <a title="litandcoffee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/82072306-litandcoffee"><img alt="litandcoffee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1526583402p2/82072306.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2442030865?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="litandcoffee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="litandcoffee" href="/user/show/82072306-litandcoffee">litandcoffee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2442030865" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11182691647170227341">The Octunnumi Fosbit Files Prologue by Trevor Alan Foris is not your usual sci-fi/fantasy. The plot is one of a kind and implementation of the theme is equally unique: so much so that reading it makes you feel as if it’s written by someone from some another planet. Yes, literally!<br/><br/>The Octunnumi is an alliance of different innesomids, its main purpose is to keep all the innesomids safe. The inhabitants of Octunnumi have special abilities and are able to visit any myth, fantasy, and make believe. T</span>
  <span id="freeText11182691647170227341" style="display:none">The Octunnumi Fosbit Files Prologue by Trevor Alan Foris is not your usual sci-fi/fantasy. The plot is one of a kind and implementation of the theme is equally unique: so much so that reading it makes you feel as if it’s written by someone from some another planet. Yes, literally!<br /><br />The Octunnumi is an alliance of different innesomids, its main purpose is to keep all the innesomids safe. The inhabitants of Octunnumi have special abilities and are able to visit any myth, fantasy, and make believe. The brothers, Reig and Trad with their special abilities and heightened skills travel between different innesomids by opening various access points to perform certain assignments: mainly to fix things. Nate Fosbit, a voluntary exiled member of Octunnumi, who had chosen to live in Fethrist in the past suddenly reappears with destruction at his hands and revenge on his mind. The various innesomids are at risk of being completely destroyed and it’s up to two brothers, with the help of their mother Meiegryn, the Commanding Officer of Octunnumi, Edgar Fosbit, Nate’s estranged father, and other officials of Octunnumi to get to Nate before it gets too late. <br /><br />The story is quite complicated and needs a thorough reading to get it completely. It is full of adventure: imagine having an ability to visit any fairy tale or to go back to any time period you find amusing. That’s what inhabitants of the Octunnumi are able to do. The brothers take readers on a journey filled with various adventures. Trevor, the inner voice of Reig is enthralling and makes for fascinating conversations between the brothers. Reig is practical whereas Trad is sweet though grumpy at times; not that you can blame him much considering Reig’s panache for keeping things a secret. There are too many characters: the other beings, some half living-half machines, ordinary inhabitants and bewitchers, but if you’ve patience you will get to know them in time. And the book, as the title states, is just a prologue (the whole book, yes!) so, the things should be more focused and clearer in the next in series: the actual story. <br /><br />There is one thing I would like to say: the initial journey of brothers which takes readers on various adventures is, no doubt, quite exploratory, gets tedious at times. The entry of villain though happens quite early in the story, it takes almost three quarter of book to get to start of actual destructive events. A tight editing would have made things more focused and sharper. <br /><br />Usually I’m a person who is not for movie version of books, but this book would make for a great sci-fi movie I feel; as in case of ‘The Lord of Rings’, the reading gets too tedious at times but watching the movies is solely entertaining. <br /><br />I’m tempted to say this book is not for everyone. Only if you are a hard-core sci-fi fan, you would like and appreciate the beauty of The Octunnumi Fosbit Files Prologue.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11182691647170227341" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2622936375" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2622936375" />
    <a title="Switched On" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/90441636-switched-on"><img alt="Switched On" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2622936375?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Switched On" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Switched On" href="/user/show/90441636-switched-on">Switched On</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2622936375" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12636586568575812339">This story begins innocuously enough with teenage brothers and their banter and play fighting. The main premise is soon revealed to be that a group of children is missing, so bring on suspicions of who is responsible and speculation on motives, and questions like do they even want to be found? That’s when it’s hard to tear yourself away from the immersive story Trevor Alan Foris has created. <br/><br/>There’s a part of the story where characters literally walk into and become part of a painting and that’s</span>
  <span id="freeText12636586568575812339" style="display:none">This story begins innocuously enough with teenage brothers and their banter and play fighting. The main premise is soon revealed to be that a group of children is missing, so bring on suspicions of who is responsible and speculation on motives, and questions like do they even want to be found? That’s when it’s hard to tear yourself away from the immersive story Trevor Alan Foris has created. <br /><br />There’s a part of the story where characters literally walk into and become part of a painting and that’s very much like my experience of reading this surreal tale, set in such rich landscapes. It’s like Foris has curated a whole bunch of his weirdest dreams and put them together in an exhibition that you can climb right into. By the end I’m not sure I wanted to climb out again...<br /></span>

<div id="review_2621741006" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2621741006" />
    <a title="Raven About" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/90397336-raven-about"><img alt="Raven About" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544445075p2/90397336.jpg" /></a>

This was an adventure and then some… It’s written with young adults in mind but I think we’re all young at heart if we allow ourselves to be. I really enjoyed this book for its pure escapism and creativity. The author writes in a really easily readable, accessible and engaging way that just kept me turning the pages and wanting more. I don’t want to spoil it for anyone, but one of my favourite parts was set in a series of impossible rooms full of mirrors, complete with fashion dummies that come to life and outfits that spontaneously change.   <span id="freeText16052335126879558786" style="display:none">This book was a real surprise for me.     <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2639608420" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2639608420" />
    <a title="Grady" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1362506-grady"><img alt="Grady" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442472304p2/1362506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2639608420?book_show_action=true">Dec 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grady" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grady" href="/user/show/1362506-grady">Grady</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2639608420" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2245666045461782036">‘Mr Tradien, I am not telling you, I am narrating: that’s my job.’<br/><br/>According to the little we know about him/her, author Trevor Alan Foris is ‘currently halfway through the second of many, many books that are The Octunnumi, a just out of sight, doesn’t really exist world of mythical creatures and magic. Of course the mythical creatures take great issue with this title as they are of course not mythical at all, being the native inhabitants of the planet Earth way before – well a long time ago; and</span>
  <span id="freeText2245666045461782036" style="display:none">‘Mr Tradien, I am not telling you, I am narrating: that’s my job.’<br /><br />According to the little we know about him/her, author Trevor Alan Foris is ‘currently halfway through the second of many, many books that are The Octunnumi, a just out of sight, doesn’t really exist world of mythical creatures and magic. Of course the mythical creatures take great issue with this title as they are of course not mythical at all, being the native inhabitants of the planet Earth way before – well a long time ago; and as for magic, there is no such thing. Like the aforementioned non-mythical creatures, the abilities of the Tarelen peoples are in no way magical. After all, mind control, telepathic communication, telekinetic control over objects is no different to any one of us breathing and is that considered magic? No, of course not, although a rock might disagree.’<br /><br />A richly colorful – both verbally and visually- epic novel seems daunting at first, but the author seems to be giving us permission to lose time and place and sense and reason and juts string along with the wild meanderings this story presents. <br /><br />Perhaps the best introduction to the lyrical writing by Trevor is to offer the opening lines of the book for an appreciation of the style and color in store: ‘Are you insane?’ Octunnumi Alliance Operatives, Reigous Sedwint Eniexous and Tradien Everwick Thivimus, currently enjoying their most recent regeneration as eighteen year-olds for the umpteenth time, crouch, their backs against one of the many concrete pillars that support the crumbling roof of the abandoned warehouse. Through the gloom, overturned boxes, crates, tables and chairs that lie scattered about the vast space are highlighted by the purple moonlight filtering through the begrimed windows high above them. ‘We don’t have time for this, Trad,’ Reig continues in a hissed whisper to his twin. ‘If she finds out—’ ‘Relax,’ Trad replies, flicking his hand in the direction of a stack of large crates opposite them. When they collapse and reveal nothing, he grumbles, ‘Dammit, I could have sworn…’ ‘Relax!’ Reig exclaims. ‘You’ve brought us to an Innesomid we are not supposed to be in, slap in the middle of a... a…’ streaks of white light zap around them, dislodging Reig’s hat and sending it spinning on its side across the floor. Rolling his eyes, he continues, ‘… a war zone, when we should in fact be heading to Fethrist, also an Innesomid not on our to do list, I might add, but given where we actually are, that would be preferable.’’<br /><br />Too ominous to summarize, the following hints at the flow of the book’s content – The Octunnumi is an alliance of individuals who have unique powers, that are used to protect the Innesomids, which are territories that share the same time and space. 18-year-old brothers Rieg and Trad are agents of the Octunnumi, and although they leap between the Innesomids to tackle pretty minor problems, they suddenly find themselves tasked with preventing a former member from destroying everything in a heinous revenge plot. Will they succeed? Or will life be over as they know it. This is an unforgettable journey through many magnificent worlds, heading toward the ultimate confrontation with a villain set on destroying it all.<br /><br />There is a passage from Shakespeare’s Tempest that shares a similar atmosphere – ‘And like the baseless fabric of this vision, “The cloud-capped towers, the gorgeous palaces, The solemn temples, the great globe itself— Yea, all which it inherit—shall dissolve, And like this insubstantial pageant faded, Leave not a rack behind. We are such stuff As dreams are made on, and our little life Is rounded with a sleep.’ Be patient on this journey to enter another world.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2245666045461782036" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16903428458875457657" style="display:none">This book is the beginning of a series that I assume is going to be long, because the whole book is the prologue. I was shocked when I realized it wasn’t just the title, not to mention intrigued. I've been ignoring traditional novels for web novels recently because of their longevity, so I'm looking forward to the next installments in this series.<br />The book itself is pretty long, it took me a couple days to go through it and I’m usually a fast reader, but the story is interesting and I couldn’t wait to make it to the end.<br />In the story, we immediately start off with some action and we’re introduced to the brothers Trad and Reig who are Octunnumi operatives. From the first page you know this story is going to involve multiple worlds and settings, and starts with the brothers in a recent regeneration as eighteen year olds—this has happened plenty before, and will keep happening, I’m assuming well into the next installments in the series.<br />It opens with action so you’re drawn in right away, and more and more details paint the story for you as you keep on reading. The one thing I particularly love about the narrative, is that the Octunnumi go across worlds based on myths, legends and tales, and different time periods, and I’ve always had an interest in this area.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophia J." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophia J." href="/user/show/82298622-sophia-j">Sophia J.</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer1387898925487817662">I was left guessing at every page, what will happen, the next characters to be introduced, and the situations that will come up next, and it’s what I love in my stories. Right from the first page, the story introduces two characters, Trad and Reig who are siblings and operatives of the Octonnumi Alliance, right in the middle of a war. They are currently eighteen, and it’s not the first time they’ve been reincarnated as eighteen year olds. The words paint the story and the plot for you as you rea</span>
  <span id="freeText1387898925487817662" style="display:none">I was left guessing at every page, what will happen, the next characters to be introduced, and the situations that will come up next, and it’s what I love in my stories. Right from the first page, the story introduces two characters, Trad and Reig who are siblings and operatives of the Octonnumi Alliance, right in the middle of a war. They are currently eighteen, and it’s not the first time they’ve been reincarnated as eighteen year olds. The words paint the story and the plot for you as you read along. I couldn’t stop flipping because I wanted to know what would happen next and what was coming, I was kept guessing and more of the time my guesses were wrong. The story is long, though, so I had to pause for sleep, but I was right back into it the next day, and I plan to reread it once the next book in series comes out. This whole book is only the prologue, so I’m already looking forward to what happens in the next installment of this world.<br />This is a fantasy story that isn’t built like more traditional fantasies, in that it has several worlds and settings, and not just one, which means there’s world-building for more than one setting, and what I’ve seen so far was done really well. The premise is based on the Octonnumi being able to jump through worlds, myths, legends, fairy tales and time periods, and there’s nothing more exciting than a story that keeps you guessing. Just based on that, the book can also be said to contain science fiction elements, so I place it as a sci fi/fantasy.<br />The Octonnumi are fighting something, and Nate Fosbit comes out as a clear villain, a fallen Octonnumi member that’s come back for revenge, and it’s up to the Trad and Reig to stop him, with a little help along the way. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2327356695781260171">Well the blurb promised me 'next level fantasy' and it definitely delivered. For the first 100 pages, I had no idea what I was reading, but I didn't care 'The Octunummi Fosbit Files' by Trevor Alan Foris completely draws you in and confuses and intrigues you, and makes you read the next page, in th hope that you will finally get you head wrapped around the plot and concepts. Stick with it and you will get there, and be gifted with an amazing journey through time and space, whilst not actually le</span>
  <span id="freeText2327356695781260171" style="display:none">Well the blurb promised me 'next level fantasy' and it definitely delivered. For the first 100 pages, I had no idea what I was reading, but I didn't care 'The Octunummi Fosbit Files' by Trevor Alan Foris completely draws you in and confuses and intrigues you, and makes you read the next page, in th hope that you will finally get you head wrapped around the plot and concepts. Stick with it and you will get there, and be gifted with an amazing journey through time and space, whilst not actually leaving one particular spot in time and space. It's quite the head scratcher, but it is so fun, so original, and so exciting. The protagonists, Trad and Reig are brothers who can jump from world to world, which are exist in the same time and space. But, they are so relatable they help to anchor the story down and give a touch of normality to a plot that is out of this world (even though they are reincarnates). <br /><br />I would say that for a novel that seems to be aimed at the Young Adult market that it may be a little complicated for pre-teens, but other than that, this wonderful novel will surely appeal to all fans of fantasy or Sci-Fi fiction. If you are wondering if this book is the one for you, visit the official website and have a read of the large sample that is available.<br /></span>

<div id="review_2629379098" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2629379098" />
    <a title="Better Than Life" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/90444804-better-than-life"><img alt="Better Than Life" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2629379098?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Better Than Life" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Better Than Life" href="/user/show/90444804-better-than-life">Better Than Life</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2629379098" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17538298920405757581">“The Octunnumi Fosbit Files Prologue” by Trevor Alan Foris is a pure science fiction delight. He describes shifting worlds, shifting realities and shifting identities but at no point did I stop believing in the characters and think ‘no – really?’, despite how magical, mysterious and bizarre it all became. I loved how the characters all interacted with each other, especially the two main characters – a pair of teenage twin brothers. There is plenty of bickering and sarcasm throughout and the auth</span>
  <span id="freeText17538298920405757581" style="display:none">“The Octunnumi Fosbit Files Prologue” by Trevor Alan Foris is a pure science fiction delight. He describes shifting worlds, shifting realities and shifting identities but at no point did I stop believing in the characters and think ‘no – really?’, despite how magical, mysterious and bizarre it all became. I loved how the characters all interacted with each other, especially the two main characters – a pair of teenage twin brothers. There is plenty of bickering and sarcasm throughout and the author obviously doesn’t take himself too seriously. He even includes himself in the story as a narrator. <br /><br />I loved how – boom! – readers are thrown straight into the story, having to figure out what’s going on, picking up on the cues. This made the whole story into even more of an adventure for me. It’s full of strokes of genius and gets two huge thumbs up from me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17538298920405757581" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

As far as I am concerned this is a highly recommended E-Book.</span>

  <span id="freeText1218415872842144908" style="display:none">Did you know that 'Eterfret' means an aggressive from or method of confinement or restraint?<br />Well I do, and that is thanks to the handy Pronunciation and Definition Guides in 'The Octunnumi Fosbit Files Prologue' from Trevor Alan Foris, which has all the potential to become one of the next great fantasy series, rivalling the likes of The Hitchikers Guide to the Galaxy or The Expanse series of novels. Our protagonists are two brothers who spend their days leaping through a series of worlds that exist in the same time and space, going where they are needed. So much relies on the 18-year-old brothers, but with a threat like ever before facing the Innesomids, they are going to need some help along the way. Hopefully, it will be enough,,,or will the war continue into installment 2?<br />You don't often have a whole book as a prologue, but if this is just an introduction to a series, I can't wait to find out what is going to happen next. Trevor Alan Foris must have imagination that is infinite, he has already come up with so much.<br /></span>

<div id="review_2585594131" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2585594131" />
    <a title="Only the Best Books" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/75630113-only-the-best-books"><img alt="Only the Best Books" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514468550p2/75630113.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2585594131?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Only the Best Books" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Only the Best Books" href="/user/show/75630113-only-the-best-books">Only the Best Books</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2585594131" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9951397241954065750">Does fantasy fiction get more epic than this?<br/>The answer is, if it does, I've yet the read it. 'The Octunnumi' by Trevor Alan Foris it a unique fantasy novel that is fun, exciting, all kinds of epic, and so well-written. I'm not even sure how to start describing the 'out there' plot, but here it goes. The Octunnumi is an alliance of individuals who have unique powers, that are used to protect the Innesomids, which are territories that share the same time and space. Rieg and Trad are members of th</span>
  <span id="freeText9951397241954065750" style="display:none">Does fantasy fiction get more epic than this?<br />The answer is, if it does, I've yet the read it. 'The Octunnumi' by Trevor Alan Foris it a unique fantasy novel that is fun, exciting, all kinds of epic, and so well-written. I'm not even sure how to start describing the 'out there' plot, but here it goes. The Octunnumi is an alliance of individuals who have unique powers, that are used to protect the Innesomids, which are territories that share the same time and space. Rieg and Trad are members of the Octunnumi, and although they leap between the Innesomids to tackle pretty minor problems, they suddenly find themselves tasked with preventing a former member from destroying everything in a heinous revenge plot. Will they succeed? Or will life be over as they know it.<br /><br />This is not a novel to whizz through, it is one that should be carefully considered, as there is a lot going on, and lots of new concepts to get you head around. I mean imagine being able to leap into a new fantastical dimension – where anything you could imagine exists – any time you wanted to? I have another question about 'The Octunnumi'. Is Trevor Alan Foris from Earth, or even this dimension – his imagination is so vast, it is almost hard to believe that he just made it all up.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9951397241954065750" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6583525054336621147" style="display:none">Let me start by saying that The Octunnumi Fosbit Files Prologue is an absolute epic fantasy novel that you can totally lose yourself in.<br /><br />Trevor Alan Foris has created an amazing and delightful world, filled with wonderful characters and as you read you never know what’s round the next corner. This is sci-fi aimed at the young adult market but I know a few fully-grown adults who would love this as much as I did. <br /><br />To sum up in three words: what an adventure!<br /></span>

<div id="review_2533931476" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2533931476" />
    <a title="Tricia Sol" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55891499-tricia-sol"><img alt="Tricia Sol" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2533931476?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tricia Sol" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tricia Sol" href="/user/show/55891499-tricia-sol">Tricia Sol</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2533931476" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10116642718497343337">First of all, I love this book starting from the cover, to the interior and the formatting. It works really well as an ebook, but if I could have a paperback look nearly as good, I would love it. It’s unlike any book I’ve seen before, and it was the first thing to catch my attention. I think the old-journal feel of the cover and interior of the book fits the story really well, too, which just made it all the more fun to read. I felt like I got sucked into the story more.<br/>Next, the story. We open </span>
  <span id="freeText10116642718497343337" style="display:none">First of all, I love this book starting from the cover, to the interior and the formatting. It works really well as an ebook, but if I could have a paperback look nearly as good, I would love it. It’s unlike any book I’ve seen before, and it was the first thing to catch my attention. I think the old-journal feel of the cover and interior of the book fits the story really well, too, which just made it all the more fun to read. I felt like I got sucked into the story more.<br />Next, the story. We open with Trad and Reig, a pair of brothers who are also operatives of the Octunnumi. The Octunnumi have the ability to visit fairy tales, myths and legends and different time periods as they please, but of course, it’s not that simple. It’s not just for fun, they have objectives with each world jump, and you know the end game when you read up to it.<br />The story is all action and adventure, and the settings and situations change often in the book. Several more interesting characters are introduced in the story, including who I assume is the main villain, at least for the prologue, Nate Fosbit, who voluntarily left the Octunnumi, but has come back to destroy and to take revenge. Trad and Reig, with help from their mother, the villain’s estranged father and other Octunnumi officials, are there to stop him and his wave of destruction.<br />While it’s an easy read, especially since it starts off with action on the first page and introduces the story and worlds to you in bits and pieces as it moves along, so you’re not weighed down with heavy world-building, you really need to read everything to gain a clearer picture. It’s a fantasy story, written as if it’s from our reality, and the thought of the Octunnumi actually existing doesn’t seem so far out there when you read the book, it’s that good. You’d have to keep reading to get all the details, and the full picture will leave you amazed at the thought put into this series, at least it did for me. It’s a little hard to finish in one sitting since the book is so long. It took me a little over two days, but it kept me interested, so I didn’t get distracted by any other shiny books until I managed to reach the last page. It being only the prologue, I look forward to the other books in the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10116642718497343337" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Digital virtual book " href="/book/show/40034713-the-octunnumi-fosbit-files-prologue">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2381524564" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10392947046545823360">First of all, this is not for everyone from the format to the premise, the whole concept is a bit ‘out there’ and not everybody is going to ‘get it’ or like it. The Octunnumi asks you to take fantasy to the next level.<br/><br/>That said I am really impressed with the presentation of this book. <br/><br/>The Octunnumi is an online publication described as ‘digital virtual book’, sample pages can be found on the 'more' page under 'sneak a peek'.<br/><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.the-octunnumi.com/more'>www.the-octunnumi.com/more</a> <br/><br/>Even if you don’t buy the book it is worth lo</span>
  <span id="freeText10392947046545823360" style="display:none">First of all, this is not for everyone from the format to the premise, the whole concept is a bit ‘out there’ and not everybody is going to ‘get it’ or like it. The Octunnumi asks you to take fantasy to the next level.<br /><br />That said I am really impressed with the presentation of this book. <br /><br />The Octunnumi is an online publication described as ‘digital virtual book’, sample pages can be found on the 'more' page under 'sneak a peek'.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.the-octunnumi.com/more">www.the-octunnumi.com/more</a> <br /><br />Even if you don’t buy the book it is worth looking just to see how beautiful it is.<br /><br />Secondly if you do buy into the premise that this book is part of our reality and from another ‘Innesomid’ (this will make sense if you read the book) then it becomes all the more engaging. <br /><br />The story line is unusual and if you like to be kept guessing from page to page then this is the book for you. <br /><br />As the title states this is the prologue, yes the whole book, and is unsurprisingly laying the foundations for subsequent books. The fantasy setting has a satisfying amount of world building throughout and whilst the end is obviously a cliff-hanger, leaving lots of unanswered questions I thoroughly enjoyed the journey into this new world.<br /><br />Update; Whilst reading this I discovered a twitter account that is linked to this story line, a sort of real time ‘companion’ book which is a novel (no pun intended) approach to widening the reach of the book also offering, I hope, a welcome bridging of the gap between this book and the next. I don’t ‘do’ social media myself but this is the account you need ‘The Conspiratorialist’ if you want to follow.</span>

<div id="review_2610792025" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2610792025" />
    <a title="Profundito" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/84279706-profundito"><img alt="Profundito" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1531831137p2/84279706.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2610792025?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Profundito" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Profundito" href="/user/show/84279706-profundito">Profundito</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2610792025" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1168895076778394500">Reading The Octunnumi by Trevor Alan Foris was an all round unique reading experience. I usually stick to actual books that I can hold, but decided to take the e-book plunge with some highly recommended fantasy fiction. What I got was a something that is hard to describe – this e-book is easily the most beautiful I have ever seen, looking like an old book that is uncovered one day in the attic that holds so many secrets that cannot be fathomed. I also loved the illustrations of cogs and wheels, </span>
  <span id="freeText1168895076778394500" style="display:none">Reading The Octunnumi by Trevor Alan Foris was an all round unique reading experience. I usually stick to actual books that I can hold, but decided to take the e-book plunge with some highly recommended fantasy fiction. What I got was a something that is hard to describe – this e-book is easily the most beautiful I have ever seen, looking like an old book that is uncovered one day in the attic that holds so many secrets that cannot be fathomed. I also loved the illustrations of cogs and wheels, intertwined with organic shapes. It draws you in and intrigues you, even before you get into the fantastical plot. I don't want to give too much away about the plot as it will take away some of the surprise, but I you want a little taster as to what it will be like, think Quantum Leap mixed with a book of Fairytale, with a touch of theoretical astrophysics added in there.<br />The Octunnumi Fosbit Files Prologue is a long book, so it does take quite the commitment, but it is worth the effort. You will get just as much out of it as much as you put into it – an unforgettable journey through many magnificent worlds, heading toward the ultimate confrontation with a villain set on destroying it all. What a read.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1168895076778394500" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2824485766" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2824485766" />
    <a title="Litnigma Reviews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/97393889-litnigma-reviews"><img alt="Litnigma Reviews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558117679p2/97393889.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2824485766?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Litnigma Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Litnigma Reviews" href="/user/show/97393889-litnigma-reviews">Litnigma Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2824485766" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5321975107221780269">It took me a while to get into this book. It's unusual, because it doesn't follow the traditional narrative arc but once I got used to this format I really loved it, not only because of the complex, original plots, but because I was constantly challenged to figure out whether what was happening in each chapter was a 'good' or a 'bad' thing. Really interesting. Worth a read. It isn't always the easiest read - at times it felt slightly alien, as if it was translated from another language. But the </span>
  <span id="freeText5321975107221780269" style="display:none">It took me a while to get into this book. It's unusual, because it doesn't follow the traditional narrative arc but once I got used to this format I really loved it, not only because of the complex, original plots, but because I was constantly challenged to figure out whether what was happening in each chapter was a 'good' or a 'bad' thing. Really interesting. Worth a read. It isn't always the easiest read - at times it felt slightly alien, as if it was translated from another language. But the author paints a wonderfully detailed and vivid picture of this world, and there's enough narrative drive to hold it together.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2631648749" />
    <a title="Minion Reviews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/80003590-minion-reviews"><img alt="Minion Reviews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522315959p2/80003590.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2631648749?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Minion Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Minion Reviews" href="/user/show/80003590-minion-reviews">Minion Reviews</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2631648749" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8592728908313634999">Reading this book is like being transported into a different universe with an ever expanding cast of characters to meet along the ride. Hold onto your hats people! This is a world where anything goes. If you can think it, it can happen. Continuous reincarnation is the norm, so, let’s say repeatedly dying due to a hazardous predilection for extreme sports, for example, isn’t a problem. This is a very playful book and very well written, by an observant author with a great sense of humor who provid</span>
  <span id="freeText8592728908313634999" style="display:none">Reading this book is like being transported into a different universe with an ever expanding cast of characters to meet along the ride. Hold onto your hats people! This is a world where anything goes. If you can think it, it can happen. Continuous reincarnation is the norm, so, let’s say repeatedly dying due to a hazardous predilection for extreme sports, for example, isn’t a problem. This is a very playful book and very well written, by an observant author with a great sense of humor who provides plenty of entertaining dialogue. Where else will you find a story with a place that is everyone’s individual version of perfection, mechanical animals, cats that can turn into jewellery and furniture that repositions and extends itself? Think The Hobbit meets Alice in Wonderland and maybe you’ll be close.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8592728908313634999" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Foris has created a world that his descriptive writing style made me forget my initial inhibitions and from the very start bought in to the interesting characters that he had created.<br/>I prefer to read in old school style from a book but the way that this story is presented mak</span>
  <span id="freeText15401560541081299408" style="display:none">I was recommended this book by a friend who usually has a good taste in books but has a preference towards the sci-fi genre. Because of this I begun this book with a degree of scepticism, unsure what I was going to unearth. Foris has created a world that his descriptive writing style made me forget my initial inhibitions and from the very start bought in to the interesting characters that he had created.<br />I prefer to read in old school style from a book but the way that this story is presented makes me wonder if it would translate as well in to a printed format.<br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2585655290" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7469935709273278006">Trad and Reig are brothers. Two normal seeming brothers who bicker relentlessly like all sibling too. However, their lives are far from what we would consider normal. They are Octunnumi agents that are tasked with visiting numerous alternative worlds – some coming straight out of fairy tales, other out of memorable myths – to fix problems and right wrongs. But, a huge challenge is coming their way. Someone from their past is determined to get their revenge, and if the brothers can't reach him in</span>
  <span id="freeText7469935709273278006" style="display:none">Trad and Reig are brothers. Two normal seeming brothers who bicker relentlessly like all sibling too. However, their lives are far from what we would consider normal. They are Octunnumi agents that are tasked with visiting numerous alternative worlds – some coming straight out of fairy tales, other out of memorable myths – to fix problems and right wrongs. But, a huge challenge is coming their way. Someone from their past is determined to get their revenge, and if the brothers can't reach him in time, then life in every alternative world could be over. The Octunnumi Fosbit Files Prologue by Trevor Alan Foris is a fantasy novel like no other. It's unique plot is full of quirky characters, action, excitement, and adventure, perfect for young adults and adults alike. <br /><br /></span>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('O4D5s/1gsfixclMaYFK1W0m7T0i9myZi9MoIg0pKZ2zpr4ngBtPsvgbbQESl4j/Zdpzf8hFH9eYCb7ljfHLalg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('EilVcifTN1f4JxnBvv7oJzGdjWbVS8+livTjBhRKxlDABiUh3GBqEU+OCp97TmKlDrod3HmXHCF8UVLmInJ7qg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer724137214275335972"><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.the-octunnumi.com/more'>www.the-octunnumi.com/more</a><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://twitter.com/TheOctunnumi'>https://twitter.com/TheOctunnumi</a><br/><br/>Trevor Alan Foris is currently halfway through the second of many, many books that are<br/>The Octunnumi, a just out of sight, doesn’t really exist world of mythical creatures and magic.<br/><br/>Of course the mythical creatures take great issue with this title as they are of course not mythical at all, being the native inhabitants of the planet Earth way</span>
  <span id="freeText724137214275335972" style="display:none"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.the-octunnumi.com/more">www.the-octunnumi.com/more</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://twitter.com/TheOctunnumi">https://twitter.com/TheOctunnumi</a><br /><br />Trevor Alan Foris is currently halfway through the second of many, many books that are<br />The Octunnumi, a just out of sight, doesn’t really exist world of mythical creatures and magic.<br /><br />Of course the mythical creatures take great issue with this title as they are of course not mythical at all, being the native inhabitants of the planet Earth way before – well a long time ago; and as for magic, there is no such thing.<br /><br />Like the aforementioned non-mythical creatures, the abilities of the Tarelen peoples are in no way magical.<br /><br />After all, mind control, telepathic communication, telekinetic control over objects is no different to any one of us breathing and is that considered magic? No, of course not, although a rock might disagree.<br /> <br />Keep tuned for more information on publication dates</span>
